U@@@ii`@TloadAtRuntimeSpecifies the map file whose contents will be referenced by this prefab.Target NameSpecifies the name by which the prefab can be referenced by entity i/o. The set of inputs the prefab has is defined by the map relays in the target map.Fixup entity namesIf enabled, any entity target names within the prefab will have a prefix applied to ensure they are unique. This prevents any issues with entities in two different prefabs having name collisions.Prefix with Target NamefixupEntityNames == false || targetName == ""If this is enabled and name fixup is enabled, the prefix used for name fixup will be the prefab target name instead of the unique id. If the target name is empty then the prefab the unique id will still be used as the prefix. Note that if two prefabs use the same target name for their prefix it will be possible to have entities inside the prefabs end up with name collisions.Load if nestedIf enabled the prefab will be loaded when it is the child of another prefab, if disabled, this prefab will not be loaded if it is the child of another prefab.If set, the contents of the prefab will not be included in visibility calculations.Display ColorA color which will be used to identify the prefab within Hammer, does not have any affect on the compiled mapCreate Prefab Runtime EntityIf enabled, there will be an entity at runtime representing this prefab as an EntityIO target. Map Relay connections will not be baked, but will instead route through this entity.Load at runtimeIf enabled the prefab will not be baked into the parent map during map compile, but instead will be dynamically loaded in the game. This requires the target map to be compiled separately. Additionally this requires support for dynamic loading of maps by the game, which may not be supported by all games and game systems. Do not use without checking to see if this is fully supported by the game you are working on.

Ð0ocbyycompression_levelCompression LevelApplies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>Specify how aggressively to attempt to reduce the memory footprint. Higher levels will try more permutations and bit rates. The higher the level, the slower the compression but the smaller the memory footprint. <br><b>NOTE</b>: Currently lowest, low and medium are all equivalent.o0TBBpBPB0B BðBPBAP@A0A AAð® `@@@8o`0zooBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@o`0zowptyy`or@0`r qxopBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@Ho`0zpowptyyvirtual_vertex_distanceVirtual Vertex DistanceApplies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/creating_a_skeleton.md<br><br>The virtual vertex distance is used by the error metric function. It will measure the error of a vertex at that particular distance from the bone in object space. This distance should be large enough to contain the vast majority of the visible vertices skinned on that particular bone. The algorithm ensures that all vertices contained up to this distance will have an error lower than the supplied error threshold in the CompressionSettings. It is generally sufficient for this value to be approximate and it is often safe to use the same value for every bone in humanoid characters. A value of 3cm (or ~1 inch in game units) is good enough for cinematographic quality for most characters. While visible vertices around the torso will often be further away than this, finger tips and facial bones will be closer than that. Because the compressed track data is stored in relative space of the parent bone, any error will accumulate down the hierarchy. This means that in order to keep the leaf bones within that accuracy threshold, all the parent bones in that chain will require even higher accuracy.opBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@o`0zowptyytranslation_constant_thresholdTranslation Constant ThresholdThreshold value to use when detecting if translation tracks are constant or default. In game units, i.e. inchesopBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@o`0zowptyyerror_thresholdError ThresholdApplies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>See :: https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/compressing_a_raw_clip.md<br><br>The last important setting to choose is the error_threshold. This is used in conjunction with the error metric and the virtual vertex distance from the skeleton in order to guarantee that a certain quality is maintained. A default value of 0.01cm (or ~0.004 inches in game units) is safe to use and it most likely should never be changed unless the units you are using differ. If you do run into issues where compression artifacts are visible, in all likelihood the virtual vertex distance used on the problematic bones is not conservative enough.opBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@o`0zowptyytracks_precisionTracks PrecisionApplies to morph animation only.<br><br>This is the per component precision threshold to try and attain when optimizing the bit rate. If the error is below the precision threshold, we will remove bits until we reach it without exceeding it. If the error is above the precision threshold, we will add more bits until we lower it underneath. 8opBBpBPB0B B{ð`pBAP@A0A AAð®{`@@@o`0z0owptyytracks_constant_thresholdTracks Constant ThresholdXo7Û```@@P,,0,&0'pP`Ú ~~RP^P1`-GM@pWPÞB4RoÛÛ(oWWPXXpXXActivityModifiertools/images/modeldoc_editor/outliner_icon_activitymodifier.pngAn extra string and weight to apply to the primary activity assigned to an animationpoN^BBpBPBpf-0B B BBAP@A0A AA0Pà¯P]-@f-@@opBBpBPBpf-0B B0j `BAP@A0A AA0Pà¯|@f-@@ opf-P--f^c^^^zHoxuyyor@0rqoPpBBpBPBpf-0B B0j `BAP@A0A AA0Pà¯|@f-@@opf-P--f^c^^^zoxuyyactivity_nameActivity Name0o0TBBpBPB0B BðBPBAP@A0A AA)4p

No scaling
Do not allow selected elements to be scaled, the parts may not fit the line exactly
Scale last
Apply scale to the last element in order to fit the line. Only proceed to scale additional elements if the scale range of the last element is not sufficient.
	SCALE_END_TO_FIT
SCALE_EQUALLY
	(Scale equally
	Attempt to apply the same amount of scale to all of the elements placed on the line while still respecting their size constraints.
SCALE_MAXIMIZE
	Maximize scale
	Each element will be scaled to is maximum allowable size that will still fit on the line.
Fit on Line Pick Mode
Specifies how a fit on line element will pick which child elements it will place.
LARGEST_FIRST
	Largest fitting
	Pick the largest child element that will fit in the remaining length of the line, repeat this process until the line is full or no child will fit in the remaining length.
	
	Random fitting
	Pick a random choice from the child elements that will fit within the remaining length, repeat this process until the line is full or no child will fit in the remaining length.
ALL_IN_ORDER
	Place all in order
	Place all of the child elements in the order they are specified even if they do not fit the line or do not fill the line. NOTE: end cap settings are ignored in this mode.(Fit on Line Scale ModeSpecifies how a fit on line element will scale generate scale values for the objects it places. |

Specifies the length of the line that will be taken up if this element is selected.fCan this object be scaled. If enabled the minimum and maximum lengths must be set to specify the size range of allowable scale.
Minimum length
m_bAllowScale == false
Minimum allowable length for the object. Must be <= length. If length is 100 and minimum length is 20, then the object may be assigned a scale in the rage [ 0.2, 1.0 ].pg-)fMaximum length
Maximum allowable length for the object. Must be >= length. If length is 100 and maximum length is 160, then the object may be assigned a scale in the rage [ 1.0, 1.6 ].pg-)fÈ¹Linear LengthSpecifies the length of this element, used when fitting an element on to a line. |

	SmartPropAttributeEditor(enum:SmartPropPathPositions_t)(È
Path Positions
	Specifies the set of positions that are valid for path placement. |
0Épg8Éf@É((HÉSpecifies the method to use to determine which positions this element should be placed at along the path.fÉ( m_PlaceAtPositions == ALL ) || ( m_PlaceAtPositions == START_AND_END ) || ( m_PlaceAtPositions == CONTROL_POINTS )Specifies the spacing between positions. For example, a value of 1 will place the element at very position, 2 every other position, 3 every third position-)ÉfÊSpecifies an offset to use when determining the Nth position to place an element at. For example if placing at every third position with an offset of 0, an element will appear at positions 1, 4, 7, and so on. But if an offset of 2 is set instead of 0, then an element will appear at positions 3, 6, and 9 and so on.-)ÊfÊShould this element be placed at the first positions on the pathfÊShould this element be placed at the last positions on the pathf ÊValid Path Positions

Name of the path to use. This path name will show up in the property editor when selecting a placement of this smart prop in Hammer, allowing selection of a path object in the map to use.
Spacing between points on the path
Offset from the start of the path to place the first point.
Offset from path
Offset to apply to the path, specifies a horizontal and vertical offset to apply relative to the up direction.
Path Evaluation Space
Specifies the space in which the provided input path is to be evalauted.
	World Space: The input path will be evaluated in world space, such that child elements will be placed directly on the target path regardless of the transform of the smart prop object. 
	Object Space: The world space transform of the input path will be ignored and instead the path will be evaluated relative to the transform of the smart prop object. Element Space: The world space transform of the input path will be ignored and instead the path will be evaluated relative to the transform of the current element within the smart prop.
	If true, treat the specified up direction as fixed up direction to apply to all elements placed on the path. If false the up direction is just an initial direction.fËCompute the spacing distance in the 2d plane defined by the up direction. Most useful when using a fixed up direction, if maintaining a distance in the 2d plane is more important than maintaing distance along the path.fËIf not using a fixed up direction, provides an initial up direction which will be used to determine the orientation of first element on the path, after that the elements will incrementally update to follow the path and may not match this direction. If Use Fixed Up direction is specified, then all elements will use this direction to deterime their up direction.fËfË
m_DefaultPathSmartPropPathPositions_t
	A set of points defining a path to use when an external path isn't specified. This will be used in the preview and thumbnail for the smart prop. It will also be used when the smart prop is placed in Hammer before a path is selected.

An element which places an instance of its child elements at a specified interval along a path. |

Fixing this error deletes the bad connections.Hidden object with no selection setA hidden object was found that does not belong to any selection sets, which is an invalid condition. Fixing this problem will hide the object in a selection set called _hidden by Check for Problems.Texture axis perpendicular to faceThe face has a texture axis that is perpendicular to the face, probably caused by rotating an object with texture locking disabled.
